## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target is dP_dt, the time-derivative of population size P(t), which is the standard setup for continuous-time population growth models in ecology. Typical relationships encode density dependence (crowding), intrinsic growth, carrying capacity limits, Allee effects, harvesting/immigration, and time-varying environments via explicit dependence on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant net flux (immigration/emigration): dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (source term plus proportional growth/decay)
- Logistic differential equation (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (linear density dependence / carrying capacity behavior)
- General quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth when c1 < 0)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density dependence shape)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric slowing near capacity)
- Richards-type (generalized logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (extra shape control for sigmoidal growth)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (low-density inhibition plus crowding limit)
- Harvesting (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (external removal independent of P)
- Harvesting (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (per-capita removal)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (time-periodic environment affecting per-capita rate)
- Time-varying carrying capacity (forced logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (seasonal resource limitation; equivalently write as c0*P*(1 - P*(c4/(1 + c5*sin(...))) ) if avoiding explicit division in implementation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth → dP_dt proportional to P (straight-line per-capita growth dP_dt/P ≈ constant).
- Carrying-capacity limitation → multiplicative crowding factor like (1 - c*P) or higher-power variants; implies dP_dt crosses zero at a finite P.
- Low-density suppression (Allee effect) → additional factor like (c*P - 1) causing dP_dt < 0 for small P and an unstable threshold.
- Asymmetric approach to capacity → log(c/P) term (Gompertz) gives stronger early growth deceleration than logistic for the same capacity.
- External inputs/removals → additive constants (±c) represent immigration/harvest independent of P; linear negative terms (−c*P) represent proportional mortality/harvest.
- Seasonality or environmental forcing → sin/cos in t multiplying P or parameters, producing oscillatory growth rate without needing extra state variables.
- Nonlinear crowding strength changes with density → exponents on P inside the crowding term (theta/Richards forms) adjust how sharply growth shuts down near capacity.
- Piecewise or regime-shift ecology (if present in data) → different parameterizations before/after a time t0, often approximated by smooth transitions using tanh(c*(t-t0)) in continuous models.

\[
f(P,t)=0.953996983528\,(1-\tfrac{P}{96.9068829767})P+0.953996983528\,P^{1/3}

This simplifies to a function of **P only**:
\[
f(P)=A\,P - \frac{A}{96.9068829767}P^2 + A\,P^{1/3},\quad A=0.953996983528
\]
So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to exactly a linear term in \(P\), a quadratic term in \(P\), and a \(P^{1/3}\) term, with **no remaining \(t\)-dependence**, and no extra functional forms (logs/exp/sin/rational in \(P\), etc.) unless they can be identically removed.

### Candidate-by-candidate analysis

1. Has \( \sin(c3 t+c4)\) in a denominator unless \(c2=0\). Then becomes \( (c0/c1)P^2 + P*c5*(1-(P c6)^{c7})^{c8}+c9P\). The middle term cannot be made into \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\) (it’s \(P\) times a non-polynomial/non-power expression unless forced constant, which would just be another \(P\) term). **No**.

2. Contains \(P^{c2}\log(\cdot)\) and \(\exp(Pc6)\). Only removable by setting coefficients \(c3=0\) and \(c5=0\), leaving just \(P^2c0+Pc1+c7\). Missing \(P^{1/3}\). **No**.

3. Same issue as (2). **No**.

4. Has \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2\) plus \(c3\exp(c4\sin(\cdot))\) which depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\) (or \(c4=0\) making it constant). If \(c3=0\), we can match the three needed powers by setting:
- \(c0 = A\)
- \(c1 = -A/96.9068829767\)
- \(c2 = A\)
This exactly reproduces GT. **Yes, match**.

5. Has an extra term \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}\) which is \( \propto P^{c4+1}\). Could set \(c2=0\) to remove, but then only \(P^2\) and \(P\) remain; no \(P^{1/3}\). **No**.

8. Has a log term; to remove set \(c3=0\). Then matches as in (7). **Yes, match**.

9. Same as (8) but with \(t\) inside; set \(c3=0\). Then matches. **Yes, match**.

You could set \(c2=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\), but then you still have an unavoidable constant \(c6\) unless set \(c6=0\). That yields \(P^2, P, P^{1/3}\) only—so actually this **can** match by choosing:
- \(c0=-A/96.9068829767\)
- \(c1=A\)
- \(c2=1/3\)
- \(c3=A\)

- \(c6=0\)

**GT: 0.954*(1 - P/96.907)*P + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

The GT is a sum of three basis functions: **P^(1/3), P, and P²**, with no dependence on t.
